< Review>
I went for a weekly rental on a hybrid. The bike I received was patently unsafe and in terrible condition. The rear wheel was severely warped. The tires were underinflated. Both brakes were so soft that stopping quickly was impossible (the warped rear wheel makes functioning brakes impossible). The derailleur was not functioning properly, gears did not stay in place and would rattle loudly. The entire drive train looked like it hadn't been lubricated in a year.
This was the only hybrid they had in my size, so I went and found a much better hybrid at another shop for only a few extra dollars. I returned the bike after a few hours on the first day. Out of a $72 rental, I received only a $33 refund. I wouldn't mind a nominal fee, but charging me nearly $40 for an unsafe bike is terrible business practice.<//Review>

<Review>BE CAREFUL buying here. Do your research on this place. As another reviewer said, "nice people, terrible service." This about sums it up. The people are all very nice and make you feel welcome. The actual service (so far) has been awful.

Why? They sold me a bike with a poorly chosen/installed component that broke and damaged the fork, then chose to take zero responsibility for it and essentially told me it wasn't their fault (I had owned it for a week and rode it only 7 miles, 6.9 of which were after the damage occurred). They then told me that don't accept returns (even if the reason for the return was their fault, like in my case) and told me my options were to exchange it for a more expensive bike (how convenient) or go buy nail polish and paint it myself. And I had paid them for the Velocare bike insurance, too. I mean, are you kidding me? Take responsibility for your store and your inventory, Trek. I made the mistake of trusting them, and it might've landed me in a potentially very costly long-term situation. I hope I'm an outlier and that they are otherwise accommodating, but who knows. Fingers crossed for better customer service in the future.

All that said, do your research before buying. Also, when you're in the shop, make sure the bike they're selling you is put together correctly. Dealing with them will be a nightmare if not.
